              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer630768006">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12873500857011874736">I been eying Dean Koontz's books since last month and Strangers was the first book I picked. The cover and the title was catchy which made me reserved it while I checked his other books. And it really captured me soon as I started reading. Actually, this might be the only thick book I read without skipping some of its pages. Yes, it was impossible to put it down and miss the little details. <br /><br />The story really gives me creeps but I also got excited to know how their nocturnal ordeals, dreams, or th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12873500857011874736">I been eying Dean Koontz's books since last month and Strangers was the first book I picked. The cover and the title was catchy which made me reserved it while I checked his other books. And it really captured me soon as I started reading. Actually, this might be the only thick book I read without skipping some of its pages. Yes, it was impossible to put it down and miss the little details. <br /><br />The story really gives me creeps but I also got excited to know how their nocturnal ordeals, dreams, or their psychotic behaviors are connected. By how he relates it to one another was way damn good. <br /><br />But, as soon as I reached the third part of the book when they started remembering what happened that night at the Tranquility Hotel, I got little disappointed. Gone with those sleepless nights when I helplessly tried to finish reading it for the extraterrestrial creatures made it dreary. Really, I didn't even think of aliens as reasons why they're being brainwashed. I was guessing it could have something like a monster or ghost. If it is something like that, I'd love to see my skin pricked with fear at night. <br /><br />Also, I don't like how it dramatically ends though I liked the lessons about faith, friendship and survival but like I said too much drama at the end. <br /><br />I gave four stars coz I truly enjoyed reading it from first till second part, but loses the fifth star when I got to the third. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2825158-kevin?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer74045515">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16356650265298417586">Strangers <br /><br />Strangers is a story about friendship, inner strength and survival. Dean Koontz manages to weave a complex tale filled with many colorful characters. <br /><br />(There are nine main characters and two sub-characters to keep track of in this lengthy novel). <br /><br />A roadside motel and its neighboring diner are the main backdrop for the story, but Mr. Koontz manages to take us coast to coast as the plot unfolds. Somehow, a group of complete strangers seems connected though none can remember ever having me</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16356650265298417586">Strangers <br /><br />Strangers is a story about friendship, inner strength and survival. Dean Koontz manages to weave a complex tale filled with many colorful characters. <br /><br />(There are nine main characters and two sub-characters to keep track of in this lengthy novel). <br /><br />A roadside motel and its neighboring diner are the main backdrop for the story, but Mr. Koontz manages to take us coast to coast as the plot unfolds. Somehow, a group of complete strangers seems connected though none can remember ever having met. The roadside motel is the common factor each of the characters share. <br /><br />The book moves at a very good pace. The 698-page length seemed like 300 pages. I could not put the book down. I read the Berkley paper back, which contains a nice afterward from the author, this proved insightful and humorous, completely on par when concerning Mr. Koontz. <br /><br />I highly recommend this novel.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/189235052?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5876717-katie" class="user" title="Katie">Katie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5876717-katie?shelf=my-bookshelf" class="actionLinkLite">my-bookshelf</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer189235052">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6319922511078905797">This book has been staring at me from my bookshelf for a long time. I am a big fan of Koontz's writing, but sometimes I can be disappointed. However, this was one of his older books, so I figured I'd give it a try, all 600+ pages. This book takes on the story of a handful of characters who are having similar dreams and visions about something they can not remember that has happened to them. Each chapter/part in the book is told by each character, which makes it easy to follow, as there are so ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6319922511078905797">This book has been staring at me from my bookshelf for a long time. I am a big fan of Koontz's writing, but sometimes I can be disappointed. However, this was one of his older books, so I figured I'd give it a try, all 600+ pages. This book takes on the story of a handful of characters who are having similar dreams and visions about something they can not remember that has happened to them. Each chapter/part in the book is told by each character, which makes it easy to follow, as there are so many. You want to keep reading so you can eventually find out what all these strangers have in common and what really did happen to them. Even though Koontz took this story to a genre I am not very interested in, the way he approached and explained it held my interest. If you are a fan of his writing then I do recommend you read this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6319922511078905797">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12409877736507168859">This was a good book, but I really think that it could have been half as long. While the plot was good and I really enjoyed the characters, there were times that I wished the book was over already. When it was finished, I was glad!<br /><br /><strong>Publisher's Summary</strong><br /><br />They were strangers.....<br />A handful of people, from different backgrounds, living in different towns and cities across America, they had nothing in common - except fear.<br /><br />They were victims....<br />Cold and stark, an unknown terror gripped their dreams and turned their days into living nightmares.<br /><br />They were chosen....<br />And they could not escape. Deep in the heart of a sprawling desert, a dark memory called out to them, drawing them to the Tranquility Motel - where the terrifying truth was waiting.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3493849177623675515">I have been listening to this book over the past couple of weeks. I enjoyed the story and the characters, but I felt that the descriptions of the characters were repeated too often. After the third time of hearing that the general is a hard-a55, I felt like shaking my I-Pod and screaming at the inanimate object, "I GET IT ALREADY! GET ON WITH THE STORY!"<br /><br />However, I think my annoyance had a lot to do with the fact that I always wanted to know what was going to happen next. Even with the repetition</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3493849177623675515">I have been listening to this book over the past couple of weeks. I enjoyed the story and the characters, but I felt that the descriptions of the characters were repeated too often. After the third time of hearing that the general is a hard-a55, I felt like shaking my I-Pod and screaming at the inanimate object, "I GET IT ALREADY! GET ON WITH THE STORY!"<br /><br />However, I think my annoyance had a lot to do with the fact that I always wanted to know what was going to happen next. Even with the repetition, I would recommend this science fiction book for anyone who still holds onto hope for the human race.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5xBaJlX4AcAbyoBCseOUlkfJmSDI8VoSAaFQlDggq2iCxGX1pyoVOpcS9PnPgnIkDj5aOYEsHbhrqFUG9LVdLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cWtID8gJatA67I8mV5YjMDjDnzgqesPmlx/dQxRzb0QUv3fcOtt+KrY0+50p98WCcTRcIWOnhEz9FtjR2OaZAQ==')})
  }

But someone has a plan to shake up Borrego that involves controlling the minds&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText6296397911180996844\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Borrego looks like an ordinary New Mexico town: it borders an Indian reservation, its teenagers are bored and restless, and its only industry is the outdated oil refinery. But someone has a plan to shake up Borrego that involves controlling the minds of the local residents. When Judith Sheffield is asked to return to her sleepy hometown to teach high school math, she discovers that the students\' mandatory flu shots don\'t really contain flu vaccine. The teacher joins forces with refinery worker Frank Arnold; his teenage son, Jed, whose mother belonged to the neighboring tribe; and Brown Eagle, the boy\'s grandfather, to find out what and who is behind the flu-shot edict and an equally mysterious takeover bid for the oil refinery.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"6296397911180996844\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent($(this));; return     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9355.Dean_Koontz">About Dean Koontz</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/9355.Dean_Koontz"><img alt="9355" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1341717803p2/9355.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14895692394084438499">Acknowledged as "America's most popular suspense novelist" (Rolling Stone) and as one of today's most celebrated and successful writers, Dean Ray Koontz has earned the devotion of millions of readers around the world and the praise of critics everywhere for tales of character, mystery, and adventure that strike to the core of what it means to be human.<br /><br />Dean R. Koontz has also published under the na</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14895692394084438499">Acknowledged as "America's most popular suspense novelist" (Rolling Stone) and as one of today's most celebrated and successful writers, Dean Ray Koontz has earned the devotion of millions of readers around the world and the praise of critics everywhere for tales of character, mystery, and adventure that strike to the core of what it means to be human.<br /><br />Dean R. Koontz has also published under the names <a title="Leigh Nichols" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/215502.Leigh_Nichols">Leigh Nichols</a>, <a title="Brian Coffey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151901.Brian_Coffey">Brian Coffey</a>, <a title="David Axton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/223718.David_Axton">David Axton</a>, <a title="Owen West" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5141372.Owen_West">Owen West</a>, <a title="Deanna Dwyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1410693.Deanna_Dwyer">Deanna Dwyer</a> and <a title="Aaron Wolfe" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1313037.Aaron_Wolfe">Aaron Wolfe</a>.<br /><br />Dean lives in Southern California with his wife, Gerda, their golden retriever, Anna, and the enduring spirit of their golden, Trixie.<br /><br /><strong>ASHLEY BELL arrives January 2016.</strong><br /><br /><strong>SAINT ODD is now available!</strong><br /><br />Facebook: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/DeanKoontzOfficial" target="_blank">Facebook.com/DeanKoontzOfficial</a><br />Twitter: @DeanKoontz<br />Website: DeanKoontz.com </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14895692394084438499">...more</a>

    </div>
